## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the core problem of population dynamics. The target variable is the right-hand side of an ODE governing population change, and classical ecological models provide many functional forms for this.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/population modeling)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic minus catabolic terms)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Logistic with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (logistic with time-modulated intrinsic rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial expansion of per-capita growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality dP_dt ~ P → exponential/Malthusian regime indicating no density dependence
- Quadratic term P*(1 - cP) = cP - cP² → logistic-type density dependence with a single stable equilibrium
- Cubic terms in P (e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)) → Allee effect with bistability and a critical population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling P*log(K/P) → Gompertz-type dynamics with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → Beverton-Holt type saturating density dependence, softer than logistic
- Explicit time dependence in growth rate → non-autonomous dynamics, possibly seasonal or environmental forcing
- Power-law P**c with c≠1 → allometric scaling of metabolic or reproductive rates with body/population size
- Product of multiple (P - threshold) factors → multiple equilibria and complex stability landscape
- Negative leading coefficient on highest power of P → bounded population with stable upper equilibrium

# Analysis of Ground Truth

The GT expression is:
$$f(t,P) = 0.1728(1 - P/48.55)P + \frac{0.1728 \cdot P}{1 + \exp(-1.524(-0.924 + P))}$$

Let me expand this:
$$f(t,P) = 0.1728P - \frac{0.1728}{48.55}P^2 + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(-1.524P + 1.408)}$$

Key observations:
- The GT has **no dependence on t** (the variable t doesn't appear)
- It contains a $P^2$ term, a $P$ term, and a sigmoid-like term $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\cdot)}$

The sigmoid term $\frac{P}{1+\exp(-aP+b)}$ needs to be matched. Let me think about how $\tanh$ relates to the sigmoid:

$$\sigma(x) = \frac{1}{1+e^{-x}} = \frac{1+\tanh(x/2)}{2}$$

So: $\frac{P}{1+e^{-x}} = P \cdot \frac{1+\tanh(x/2)}{2} = \frac{P}{2} + \frac{P}{2}\tanh(x/2)$

Where $x = -1.524(-0.924 + P) = 1.524 \cdot 0.924 - 1.524P$

So $\frac{0.1728P}{1+e^{-x}} = 0.0864P + 0.0864P\tanh(x/2)$

where $x/2 = 0.762P \cdot 0.924/2 - 0.762P = -0.762P + 0.704$... let me redo:

$x/2 = (-1.524P + 1.408)/2 = -0.762P + 0.704$

Wait, $x = 1.524P - 1.408$ (checking sign): $-1.524 \cdot (-0.924 + P) = 1.524 \cdot 0.924 - 1.524P = 1.408 - 1.524P$

So $x/2 = 0.704 - 0.762P$

Therefore: GT = $-0.003559P^2 + 0.1728P + 0.0864P + 0.0864P\tanh(0.704 - 0.762P)$
$= -0.003559P^2 + 0.2592P + 0.0864P\tanh(-0.762P + 0.704)$

This is of the form: $c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + c_2 P \tanh(c_3 P + c_4)$

Now let me check candidates:

## Checking Candidate 25: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2\tanh(Pc_3 + c_4)$

This is exactly the form I derived! Setting:
- $c_0 = -0.003559$
- $c_1 = 0.2592$
- $c_2 = 0.0864$
- $c_3 = -0.762$
- $c_4 = 0.704$

This matches the GT perfectly! ✓

Let me verify there's no t-dependence issue. The GT has no t-dependence, and candidate 25 has no t-dependence. ✓

## Quick check on other candidates

Many other candidates (24, 26, 21, 22, etc.) are equivalent to candidate 25 since they have redundant terms that can be absorbed. But the key finding is candidate 25 matches exactly.

For example:
- **Candidate 24**: $P^2c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2\tanh(Pc_3+c_4) + Pc_5$ — equivalent to 25 with $c_5$ absorbed into $c_1$. ✓
- **Candidate 20**: adds constant $c_5$ — would need $c_5=0$. ✓
- **Candidate 21**: $P^2(c_0+c_1) + Pc_2 + Pc_3\tanh(Pc_4+c_5)$ — same form. ✓

Many candidates match, but the cleanest match is **Candidate 25**.
